<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=center>NOTICE OF NO AUDITOR REVIEW OF INTERIM FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Under National Instrument 51-102, Part 4, subsection 4.3(3)(a), if an auditor has not performed a review of the interim financial statements, they must be accompanied by a notice indicating that the financial statements have not been reviewed by an auditor.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The accompanying unaudited interim financial statements of Alberta Star Development Corp. (the &#147;Company&#148;) have been prepared by and are the responsibility of the Company&#146;s management. &nbsp;The unaudited interim financial statements are prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in Canada and reflect management&#146;s best estimates and judgements based on information currently available.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s independent auditor has not performed a review of these interim financial statements in accordance with standards established by the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants for a review of interim financial statements by an entity&#146;s auditor.</P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36.467px; text-indent:-36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>1.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Nature and Continuance of Operations</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Alberta Star Development Corp. (the &#147;Company&#148;) was incorporated under the laws of the province of Alberta on 6 September 1996 and is in the exploration stage. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company is in the business of acquiring and exploring mineral properties. &nbsp;The recoverability of the amounts expended by the Company on acquiring and exploring mineral properties is dependent upon the existence of economically recoverable reserves, the ability of the Company to complete the acquisition and/or development of the properties and upon future profitable production.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company&#146;s financial statements as at 31 August 2009 and for the period then ended have been prepared on a going concern basis, which contemplates the realization of assets and the settlement of liabilities and commitments in the normal course of business. &nbsp;The Company has a loss of $2,685,282 for the nine month period ended 31 August 2009 (31 August 2008 - $5,193,345) and has working capital of $13,803,608 at 31 August 2009 (31 August 2008 - $17,638,358, 30 November 2008 - $15,655,748).</P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>&nbsp;</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company had cash and cash equivalents of $15,354,479 at 31 August 2009 (31 August 2008 - $19,390,530, 30 November 2008 - $17,367,576), but management cannot provide assurance that the Company will ultimately achieve profitable operations or become cash flow positive, or raise additional debt and/or equity capital. &nbsp;However, based on its prior demonstrated ability to raise capital, management believes that the Company&#146;s capital resources should be adequate to continue operating and maintain its business strategy during fiscal 2009. &nbsp;However, if the Company is unable to raise additional capital in the future, management expects that the Company will need to curtail operations, liquidate assets, seek additional capital on less favourable terms and/or pursue other remedial measures. &nbsp;These financial statements do not include any adjustments related to the recoverability and classification of assets or
 the amounts and classification of liabilities that might be necessary should the Company be unable to continue as a going concern.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36.467px; text-indent:-36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Changes in Accounting Policies and Presentation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Effective 1 December 2008, the Company adopted the Canadian Institute of Chartered Accountants (&#147;CICA&#148;) Handbook Section 3064 &#147;<I>Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets</I>&#148;. &nbsp;The new requirements of Section 3064 are for recognition, measurement, presentation and disclosure. &nbsp;Section 3064 replaces Section 3062, &#147;<I>Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets</I>&#148;. The new standard establishes revised standards for the recognition, measurement, presentation and disclosure of goodwill and intangible assets. The new standard also provides guidance for the treatment of preproduction and start-up costs and requires that these costs be expensed as incurred. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>In 2001, the CICA issued Accounting Guideline No. 11, which covers the Company&#146;s exploration activities. &nbsp;In the past, the Company has capitalized certain exploration costs on mineral properties that were not covered by feasibility studies, whereas under the new guideline, the Company was required to expense these amounts in the year incurred. &nbsp;Effective 1 January 2001, the Company adopted these new recommendations on a retroactive basis. &nbsp;The impact as at 1 January 2001 of the adoption of these new recommendations was to reduce mineral properties by $561,257 and to increase deficit, accumulated during the exploration stage by $561,257.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>(7)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36.467px; text-indent:-36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>3.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Significant Accounting Policies</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The accounting policies of the Company are in accordance with Canadian generally accepted accounting principles (&#147;Canadian GAAP&#148;). &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Cash and cash equivalents</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Cash and cash equivalents include highly liquid investments with original maturities of three months or less.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Property, plant and equipment</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Property, plant and equipment are recorded at cost and are amortized over their estimated useful lives at 20% to 30%, with exception to computer software which is amortized at 100%, and half the rate being applied in the year of acquisition.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt">Amortization of assets used in exploration is expensed to mineral properties expenditures.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Mineral properties and deferred exploration costs</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Mineral exploration costs and option maintenance payments are expensed as incurred. &nbsp;When it has been determined that a mineral property can be economically developed as a result of establishing proven and probable reserves, costs incurred prospectively to develop the property are capitalized as incurred and are depreciated using the unit-of-production depreciation method over the estimated life of the ore body based on proven and probable reserves.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Major development costs incurred after the commencement of production, are capitalized as incurred and are depreciated using the unit-of-production depreciation method based on proven and probable reserves.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Ongoing development expenditures to maintain production are charged to operations as incurred.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Mineral property, deferred exploration costs and option maintenance payments are currently charged to operations as incurred since the Company has not met the criteria for deferral of acquisition and development costs under Canadian GAAP.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Although the Company has taken steps to verify title to mineral properties in which it has an interest, according to the usual industry standards for the stage of exploration of such properties, these procedures do not guarantee the Company&#146;s title. &nbsp;Such properties may be subject to prior agreements or transfers and title may be affected by undetected defects.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(8)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Unaudited)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Reclamation costs</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company&#146;s policy for recording reclamation costs is to record a liability for the estimated costs to reclaim mined land by recording charges to production costs for each tonne of ore mined over the life of the mine. &nbsp;The amount charged is based on management&#146;s estimation of reclamation costs to be incurred. &nbsp;The accrued liability is reduced as reclamation expenditures are made. &nbsp;Certain reclamation work is performed concurrently with mining and these expenditures are charged to operations at that time.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Stock-based compensation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Effective 1 December 2002, the Company adopted, on a prospective basis, the provisions of the CICA Handbook Section 3870, &#147;<I>Stock-Based Compensation and Other Stock Based Payments</I>&#148;, which establishes standards for the recognition, measurement and disclosure of stock-based compensation and other stock-based payments to both employees and non-employees. &nbsp;Section 3870 recommends that certain stock-based transactions, such as the grant of stock options, be accounted for at fair value. &nbsp;The Company uses the Black-Scholes option pricing model to estimate the fair value of each stock option at the granted date. &nbsp;Any consideration received from the exercise of stock options is credited to share capital. &nbsp;This section is only applicable to transactions that occurred on or after 1 December 2002.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Loss per share</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Basic loss per share is calculated based on the weighted average number of shares outstanding during the period. The treasury stock method is used for determining the dilutive effect of options and warrants issued in calculating diluted earnings per share. &nbsp;Under this method, the dilutive effect on loss per share is recognized on the use of the proceeds that could be obtained upon exercise of options, warrants and similar instruments. &nbsp;It assumes that the proceeds would be used to purchase common shares at the average market price during the year. &nbsp;For the periods presented, this calculation proved to be anti-dilutive.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Impairment of long-lived assets</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Long-lived assets are reviewed for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may not be recoverable. &nbsp;An impairment loss would be recognized when the carrying amount of an asset exceeds the estimated undiscounted future cash flows expected to result from the use of the asset and its eventual disposition. &nbsp;The amount of the impairment loss to be recorded is calculated by the excess of the assets carrying value over its fair value. &nbsp;Fair value is determined using a discounted cash flow analysis. </P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(9)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>

<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Asset retirement obligation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Effective 1 December 2004, the Company adopted the recommendations of CICA Handbook Section 3110, &#147;<I>Asset Retirement Obligations&#148;</I>. &nbsp;This section requires recognition of a legal liability for obligations relating to retirement of property, plant and equipment, and arising from the acquisition, construction, development or normal operation of those assets. &nbsp;Such asset retirement cost must be recognized at fair value in the period in which it is incurred, added to the carrying value of the asset, and amortized into income on a systematic basis over its useful life. &nbsp;Adoption of this standard has not affected the Company&#146;s financial statements.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Flow-through common shares</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has financed a portion of its exploration activities through the issue of flow-through shares, which transfers the income tax deductibility of exploration expenditures to the investor. &nbsp;Proceeds received on the issue of such shares have been credited to share capital and the related exploration costs have been charged to exploration properties and deferred exploration expenditures. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company follows the recommendations of the Emerging Issues Committee (&#147;EIC&#148;) of the CICA with respects to flow-through shares, as outlined in EIC-146. &nbsp;The application of EIC-146 requires the recognition of the foregone tax benefit on the date the Company renounces the tax credits associated with the exploration expenditures, provided there is reasonable assurance that the expenditures will be made. &nbsp;The recommendations apply to all flow-through share transactions initiated after 19 March 2004.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Income taxes</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Future income tax assets and liabilities are determined based on temporary differences between the accounting and the tax bases of the assets and liabilities and for loss carry forwards and are measured using the tax rates expected to apply when these differences reverse. &nbsp;A valuation allowance is recorded against any future income tax asset if it is not more likely than not that the asset will be realized. &nbsp;As at 30 November 2008, the Company&#146;s net future income tax assets are fully offset by a valuation allowance.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Foreign currency translation</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Revenue and expenses are translated at the exchange rates prevailing at the transactions dates. &nbsp;Transaction amounts denominated in foreign currencies are translated into functional currency at exchange rates prevailing at transaction dates.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Use of estimates</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The preparation of financial statements in conformity with Canadian GAAP requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosures of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenditures during the reported period. &nbsp;Actual results could differ from these estimates.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(10)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Unaudited)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Values</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The amounts shown for mineral properties and for deferred exploration costs represent costs to date, and do not necessarily represent present or future values, as they are entirely dependent upon the economic recovery of future reserves.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Financial Instrument Standards</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Effective 1 December 2006, the Company adopted the new CICA Handbook Section 3855, &#147;<I>Financial Instruments &#150; Recognition and Measurement</I>&#148;; Section 3865, &#147;<I>Hedges</I>&#148;; Section 1530, &#147;<I>Comprehensive Income</I>&#148;; and Section 3861, &#147;<I>Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosure and Presentation</I>&#148; (the &#147;Financial Instrument Standards&#148;). &nbsp;Effective 1 December 2007, the Company adopted the new CICA Handbook Section 3862, <I>&#147;Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosures&#148;</I> and Section 3863, <I>&#147;Financial Instruments &#150; Presentation&#148;</I> which replace existing Section 3861, <I>&#147;Financial Instruments &#150; Disclosure and Presentation&#148;</I>, revising and enhancing its disclosure requirements, and carrying forward unchanged its presentation requirements. &nbsp;These new sections place increased emphasis on disclosures about the nat
ure and extent of risks arising from financial instruments and how the entity manages those risks. &nbsp;These new standards have been adopted on a prospective basis with no restatement to prior period financial statements.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Financial Instrument Standards require that adjustments to the carrying value of financial assets and liabilities be recorded within retained earnings or, in the case of available-for-sale assets, accumulated other comprehensive income on transition. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:60px; text-indent:-24px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The principal changes resulting from the adoption of the Financial Instrument Standards are as follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:60px; text-indent:-24px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Financial Assets and Financial Liabilities</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Under the new standards, financial assets and liabilities are initially recognized at fair value and are subsequently measured based on their classification as held-to-maturity, loans and receivables, available-for-sale or held-for-trading, as described below. &nbsp;The classification is not changed subsequent to initial recognition. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Held-to-Maturity and Loans and Receivables</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Financial instruments that have a fixed maturity date, where the Company intends and has the ability to hold to maturity are classified as held-to-maturity and measured at amortized cost using the effective interest rate method. &nbsp;Loans and receivables are measured at amortized cost using the effective interest method.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Available-for-Sale</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Financial assets classified as available-for-sale are carried at fair value (where determinable based on market prices of actively traded securities) with changes in fair value recorded in other comprehensive income. &nbsp;Available-for-sale securities are written down to fair value through earnings whenever it is necessary to reflect an other-than-temporary impairment. &nbsp;Transaction costs that are directly attributable to the acquisition or issue of a financial asset or financial liability are added to its fair value. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(11)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Unaudited)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Held-for-Trading</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Financial assets and financial liabilities that are purchased and incurred with the intention of generating profits in the near term are classified as held-for-trading. &nbsp;These instruments are measured at fair value with the change in the fair value recognized in income.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Derivatives and Hedge Accounting</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company does not hold or have any exposure to derivate instruments and accordingly is not impacted by CICA Handbook Section 3865, &#147;<I>Hedges</I>&#148;.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify><I>Comprehensive Income</I></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Comprehensive income is composed of the Company&#146;s earnings and other comprehensive income. &nbsp;Other comprehensive income includes unrealized gains and losses on available-for-sale securities, foreign currency translation gains and losses on the net investment in self-sustaining operations and changes in the fair market value of derivate instruments designated as cash flow hedges, all net of income taxes. &nbsp;Cumulative changes in other comprehensive income are included in accumulated other comprehensive income which is presented (if applicable) as a new category in shareholders&#146; equity.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Comparative figures</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt">Certain comparative figures have been adjusted to conform to the current period&#146;s presentation. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>International Financial Reporting Standards (&#147;IFRS&#148;)</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>In 2006, the Canadian Accounting Standards Board (&#147;AcSB&#148;) published a new strategic plan that will significantly affect financial reporting requirements for Canadian companies. The AcSB strategic plan outlines the convergence of Canadian GAAP with IFRS over an expected five year transitional period. In February 2008, the AcSB announced that 2011 is the changeover date for publicly-listed companies to use IFRS, replacing Canada&#146;s own GAAP. The date is for interim and annual financial statements relating to fiscal years beginning on or after 1 January 2011. The transition date of 1 January 2011 will require the restatement for comparative purposes of amounts reported by the Company for the year ended 30 November 2011. While the Company has begun assessing the adoption of IFRS for 2011, the financial reporting impact of the transition to IFRS cannot be reasonably estimated at this time.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(12)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36.467px; text-indent:-36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>4.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Fair Value of Financial Instruments</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company&#146;s financial instruments consist of cash and cash equivalents, amounts receivable, and accounts payable and accrued liabilities. &nbsp;Unless otherwise noted, it is management&#146;s opinion that the Company is not exposed to significant interest, currency or credit risks arising from their financial instruments. &nbsp;The fair value of these financial instruments approximates their carrying values, due to their short-term maturity or capacity of prompt liquidation.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36.467px; text-indent:-36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>5.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Amounts Receivable </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt">Amounts receivable are non-interest bearing, unsecured and have settlement dates within one year.</P>

<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Unaudited)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36px; text-indent:-36px; font-size:11pt"><B>7.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Mineral Properties</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt"><B>Contact Lake Property &#150; Contact Lake, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2005, the Company acquired a 100% undivided right, title and interest, subject to a 1% net smelter return royalty (&#147;NSR&#148;), in five mineral claims, totalling 1,801.82 hectares (&#147;ha&#148;) (4,450.50 acres) located five miles southeast of Port Radium on Great Bear Lake, Northwest Territories (&#147;NT&#148;), for cash payments of $60,000 (paid) and 300,000 common shares (issued and valued at $72,000) of the Company. &nbsp;The Company may purchase the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000. &nbsp;The Company completed additional staking in the area in order to increase the project size to sixteen contiguous claims, totalling 10,563.76 ha (26,103.52 acres). &nbsp;Collectively the properties are known as the Contact Lake Mineral Claims.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt">Expenditures related to the Contact Lake Mineral Claims can be summarized as follows:</P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Port Radium &#150; Glacier Lake Property, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2005, the Company acquired a 100% undivided right, title and interest, subject to a 2% NSR, in four mineral claims, totalling 2,520.78 ha (6,229.00 acres) (the &#147;Glacier Lake Mineral Claims&#148;) located one mile east of Port Radium on Great Bear Lake, NT, for cash payments of $30,000 (paid) and 360,000 common shares (issued and valued at $72,000) of the Company. &nbsp;The Company may purchase one-half of the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000.</P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Port Radium &#150; Crossfault Lake Property, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2005, the Company acquired a 100% undivided right, title and interest, subject to a 2% NSR, in five mineral claims, totalling 1,820.56 ha (4,498.68 acres) (the &#147;Port Radium &#150; Crossfault Lake Mineral Claims&#148;) located north of Port Radium on Great Bear Lake, NT, for cash payments of $60,000 (paid) and 450,000 common shares (issued and valued at $297,000) of the Company. &nbsp;The Company may purchase one-half of the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Expenditures related to the Port Radium &#150; Crossfault Lake Mineral Claims can be summarized as follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<TABLE cellSpacing=0 width="100%" border=0>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Port Radium &#150; Eldorado Property, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2005, the Company entered into a lease agreement with South Malartic Exploration Inc. to purchase a 50% undivided right, title and interest in three mineral claims, totalling 106.53 ha (263.13 acres) (the &#147;Eldorado Uranium Mineral Claims&#148;) located at Port Radium on Great Bear Lake, NT, for a cash payment of $20,000 (paid).</P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>North Contact Lake Mineral Claims &#150; Great Bear Lake, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2006, the Company acquired a 100% right, interest and title, subject to a 2% NSR, in eleven mineral claims (the &#147;North Contact Lake Mineral Claims&#148;), for cash payments of $75,000 and the issue of 250,000 common shares of the Company valued at $182,500. &nbsp;The Company may purchase one-half of the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000. &nbsp;The North Contact Lake Mineral Claims are situated north of Contact Lake on Great Bear Lake approximately 680 km (423 miles) north of Yellowknife, NT, totalling 6,305.22 ha (15,580.48 acres).</P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Eldorado South IOCG &amp; Uranium Project, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2007, the Company staked sixteen claims (the &#147;Eldorado South Uranium Mineral Claims&#148;) and four additional claims (the &#147;Eldorado West Uranium Mineral Claims&#148;) located ten miles south of the Eldorado uranium mine on the east side of Great Bear Lake, NT and 680 km (423 miles) north of the city of Yellowknife, NT, collectively known as the Eldorado South Uranium Project. The Eldorado South Uranium Project now consists of thirty mineral claims totalling 25,913.25 ha (64,032.78 acres).</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; text-indent:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Longtom Property &#150; Longtom Lake, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company holds a 50% undivided interest subject to a 2% NSR, totalling 355.34 ha (878.05 acres), in the Longtom Property (the &#147;Longtom Property&#148;) located about 350 km northwest of Yellowknife, NT. &nbsp;The Longtom Property is registered 100% in the name of the Company and the Company is the operator of the Longtom Property.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(18)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Unaudited)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has the right to acquire the remaining 50% interest in the Longtom Property (the &#147;Longtom Option&#148;) for $315,000 payable either in cash or<B> </B>50% ($157,500) in cash and 50% in common shares of the Company. &nbsp;The deemed price of the Company&#146;s shares issued on the exercise of the Longtom Option would be the average TSX Venture Exchange closing market price of its common shares on the five trading days immediately preceding and the five trading days immediately following the date that the option is exercised. The Company is compelled to exercise the Longtom Option: 1) within 90 days from the date it has incurred $5,000,000 in exploration expenditures on the Longtom Property; or 2) at the date the Company advises the optionor in writing that it will complete the Longtom Option to purchase the remaining 50% interest in the Longtom Property (Note 12).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has the right to enter into joint venture or option agreements related to the Longtom Property with third parties prior to the exercise of the Longtom Option.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>In 2003, the Company entered into a Letter of Intent (the &#147;Letter of Intent&#148;) with Fronteer Development Group Inc. (&#147;Fronteer&#148;). &nbsp;On 26 October 2006, Fronteer earned its 75% interest in the Longtom Property by paying the Company $15,000 cash (received) and spending an aggregate of $500,000 (incurred) on exploration expenditures over three years.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Longtom Property (Target 1) &#150; Longtom Lake, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2003, the Company acquired a 50% interest in a 710.67 ha (1,756.10 acres) mineral property located in the Longtom Lake area of the Northwest Territories for cash proceeds of $15,000 and 200,000 common shares of the Company valued at $56,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>MacInnis Lake Property &#150; MacInnis Lake, Northwest Territories</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>During the year ended 30 November 2005, the Company acquired a 100% interest, subject to a 2% NSR, in twelve mineral claims (the &#147;MacInnis Lake Uranium Claims&#148;) and three additional mineral claims (the &#147;Kult Claims&#148;) located approximately 275 km southeast of Yellowknife, NT, collectively known as the MacInnis Lake Uranium Project. &nbsp;The acquisition was completed for cash proceeds of $100,000 (paid) and 650,000 common shares (issued and valued at $158,000) of the Company.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The MacInnis Lake Uranium Project now consists of fifteen mineral claims totaling 10,701.16 ha (26,431.87 acres).</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt" align=right>&nbsp;(20)</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=center><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:0px; page-break-before:always" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>Alberta Star Development Corp.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:16pt; margin:0px; font-size:14pt" align=justify><B>(An Exploration Stage Company)</B></P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">Notes to Financial Statements</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Expressed in Canadian Dollars)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; font-size:12pt">(Unaudited)</P>
<P style="line-height:14pt; margin:0px; padding-bottom:4px; font-size:12pt; border-bottom:1px solid #000000"><B>31 August 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company entered into an option agreement dated 1 April 2005, as amended 11 April 2006 and again on 29 September 2008 with Max Resource Corp. (&#147;Max Resource&#148;), whereby Max Resource can earn an interest, subject to a 2% NSR, in the MacInnis Lake Uranium Project. The terms of the option agreement calls for Max Resource to make payments as follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>a.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; text-indent:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Cash payments totalling $30,000 (received);</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>b.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The issuance of 200,000 common shares of Max Resource (received and sold for proceeds of $198,466); </P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:72px; text-indent:-35.467px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>c.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:72px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Work commitments totalling $2,000,000 ($250,000 on or before 31 October 2008 (incurred); $750,000 on or before 31 October 2009 ($234,307 incurred); $500,000 on or before 31 October 2010; and $500,000 on or before 31 October 2011).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The terms of the option agreement call for Max Resource to earn a 25% interest in the MacInnis Lake Property upon making the payments in i. and ii. above together with the first $1,000,000 in work commitments. &nbsp;Max Resource may earn a further 25% interest when it completes the $2,000,000 in work commitments. &nbsp;Upon full exercise of the option, the parties agree to enter into a joint venture agreement. &nbsp;The Company is the operator of the project for the term of the option agreement. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has not conducted exploration activities during the period on this property pending the resolution of permit issues in this region.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Accounts Payable and Accrued Liabilities</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Accounts payable and accrued liabilities are non-interest bearing, unsecured and have settlement dates within one year.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Included in the accounts payable and accrued liabilities at 31 August 2009 is $639,445 (30 November 2008 - $685,941) related to Part XII.6 tax on funds raised by the Company on flow-through share offerings.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Included in the accounts payable and accrued liabilities at 31 August 2009 is $739,687 (30 November 2008 &nbsp;- $739,687) related to the estimated costs to the Company for amending its flow-through filings (Notes 10, 12 and 13).</P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Capital Stock </B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36.467px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Authorized capital stock consists of an unlimited number of voting common shares. &nbsp;Authorized capital stock also consists of an unlimited number of preferred shares, to be issued in series, with the directors being authorized to determine the designation, rights, privileges, restrictions and conditions attached to all of the preferred shares.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>Effective 10 October 2008, the Board of Directors has approved and adopted a shareholders rights plan (the &#147;Rights Plan&#148;) subject to shareholder and regulatory approval which was received on 3 February 2009. &nbsp;The Rights Plan extends the minimum expiry period for a takeover bid to 60 days and requires a bid to remain open for an additional 10 business days after an offeror publicly announces it has received tenders for more than 50% of the Company&#146;s voting shares. &nbsp;The principle purpose of the Rights Plan is to ensure that all shareholders will be treated equally and fairly in the event of a bid for control of the Company through an acquisition of its common shares. &nbsp;It is designed to provide the Company shareholders with sufficient time to properly consider a takeover bid without undue time constraints. &nbsp;In addition, it will provide the board with additional time for review and consider
ation of unsolicited takeover bids, and if necessary, for the consideration of alternatives.</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36px; text-indent:-36px; font-size:11pt"><B>12.</B></P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:71.067px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company has outstanding and future commitments under mineral property option agreements to pay cash and issue common shares of the Company (Note 7).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:71.067px; text-indent:-35.533px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>ii.</P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:71.067px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>On 1 April 2006, the Company entered into a five year lease (expires 1 March 2011) for premises with minimum lease commitments of approximately $3,575 per month.</P>

<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36px; text-indent:-36px; font-size:11pt"><B>14.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Segmented Information</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company operates solely in Canada in one reporting segment, mineral production and related activities.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-17.333px; padding-left:36px; text-indent:-36px; font-size:11pt"><B>15.</B></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt"><B>Capital Disclosures</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The capital structure of the Company consists of equity attributable to common shareholders, comprising of issued capital, contributed surplus, warrants, deficits and accumulated other comprehensive income. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s objective when managing capital are to: (i) preserve capital, (ii) obtain the best available net return and (iii) maintain liquidity.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company manages the capital structure and makes adjustments to it in light of changes in economic condition and the risk characteristics of the underlying assets. &nbsp;To maintain or adjust the capital structure, the Company may attempt to issue new shares, issue new debt, acquire or dispose of assets or adjust the amount of cash and cash equivalents and investments.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company&#146;s policy is to invest its excess cash in highly liquid, fully guaranteed, bank-sponsored instruments. This strategy is unchanged from fiscal 2008.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:13pt; margin:0px; padding-left:36px; font-size:11pt" align=justify>The Company is not subject to externally imposed capital restrictions.</P>

<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><B>OVERVIEW AND OVERALL PERFORMANCE</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Alberta Star Development Corp. is engaged in the acquisition, exploration and development of exploration properties in Canada&#146;s Northwest Territories (&#147;NT&#148;). These properties are in the exploration stage. &nbsp;The Company does not generate income or cash flow from its operations. The Company&#146;s outlook is dependent on the global demand for the minerals that it is seeking on its properties, namely copper, gold, silver, cobalt, lead, zinc and uranium.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company carried out its Phase 3, 2008 Summer Exploration Drill Program at the Company&#146;s Eldorado-Glacier Lake permit area and Contact Lake permit area from June to August consisting of a seventeen (17) hole drill program. &nbsp;During the three month program, the Company completed over 2,600 meters of drilling. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s exploration team has combined the results from the 2006-2007 drill programs, which included one hundred and nineteen (119) drill holes completed, totaling more than 33,800 meters, with the results of the 2008 drill program. The 2006 &#150; 2008 drill programs total one hundred and thirty six (136) drill holes completed, totaling 36,400 meters. </P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company did not conduct exploration in 2009 due to unfavourable market conditions and high field costs. During the Summer, the Company demobilized its exploration camp at Echo Bay, NT. &nbsp;The Company intends to monitor and provide updates on its future exploration programs as market conditions change. The Company continues to reduce its overhead and look for additional avenues to conserve its working capital with the intent to continue to develop or acquire an economic mineral deposit. The Company has a strong balance sheet and no debt and is focused on cost cutting, maintaining qualified management and developing or acquiring economic projects. As a result of the global economic crisis, there was a serious shortage of available capital and exploration risk to the resource industry, but this market situation has improved greatly. The Company intends to manage its cash resources and review opportunities as circumstances demand. &nbsp;The Company has and continues to 
conduct due diligence reviews on a number of resource opportunities, including a number of advanced stage mineral exploration projects that meet the Company&#146;s corporate mandate of acquiring opportunities with established resources, expansion potential, infrastructure, cash flow and near term cash flow.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>On June 10, 2009, the Company filed a &#147;Notice of Appearance and Request for Special Notice&#148; with the United States Bankruptcy court for the District of Idaho regarding the Sterling Silver Mining Company and its corporate assets situated in the Coeur d&#146;Alene, Idaho mining district.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>On July 3, 2009, the Company issued 3,950,000 stock options to directors, officers, employees and consultants of the Company with an exercise price of $0.20 per share for a period of five years.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>As at October 19, 2009, the Company continues to be a party of interest with the United States Bankruptcy Court for the District of Idaho in the matter regarding the Sterling Silver Mining Company and its corporate assets situated in the Coeur d&#146;Alene, Idaho mining district, Idaho, USA. &nbsp;As a party of interest, the Company is interested in pursuing options with the debtor, Sterling Mining Company and its related assets.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s shares are listed on the TSX Venture Exchange under the symbol &#147;ASX&#148;, on the OTCBB under the symbol &#147;ASXSF&#148; and on the Frankfurt Exchange under the symbol &#147;QLD&#148;.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>As at August 31, 2009 the Company had working capital of $13,803,608, inclusive of $15,354,479 of cash and cash equivalents on hand. &nbsp;Cash and cash equivalents on hand at the date of this MD&amp;A are approximately $15,000,000 which is sufficient to cover additional property acquisitions, planned exploration expenditures, and administration costs for at least 12 months.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><B>PROPERTIES</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s exploration property assets consist of:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:3.333px; margin-bottom:3.333px" align=center>3</P>
<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:3.667px; page-break-before:always" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><B>The Eldorado &amp; Contact Lake IOCG &amp; Uranium Properties:</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s property interests consist of 47,199.77 ha (116,633.17 acres), situated in the Eldorado/Port Radium/Contact Lake area, &nbsp;McKenzie Mining District, NT. &nbsp;The Company is the first mineral exploration company in 75 years to successfully stake and control this large contiguous land package in the Northwest Territories.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>In 2008, the Company completed Phase 3 of the exploratory drill program based on the investigations from the 2006 &#150; 2007 drill programs at the Eldorado/Contact Lake project area. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s main exploration camp, personnel, and supporting infrastructure were fully operational from June to August, 2008. &nbsp;The Company completed over 2,600 meters of drilling in seventeen (17) drill holes during the program. &nbsp;The 2008 drill program targeted five areas; Skinny Lake, K2, K4 &nbsp;located on the Contact Lake Mineral Claims, and Gossan Island and Long Bay located on the Glacier Lake Mineral Claims. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify><B>1.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><B>Contact Lake Mineral Claims &#150; Contact Lake, and North Contact Lake Mineral Claims &#150; Great Bear Lake, NT</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>During the year ended November 30, 2005, the Company acquired a 100% undivided right, title and interest, subject to a 1% net smelter return royalty (&#147;NSR&#148;), in five (5) mineral claims, totalling 1,801.82 ha (4,450.50 acres) located five miles southeast of Port Radium on Great Bear Lake, NT for cash payments of $60,000 (paid) and 300,000 common shares (issued and valued at $72,000) of the Company. &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company may purchase the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000. &nbsp;The Company completed additional staking in the area in order to increase the project size to sixteen (16) contiguous claims, totalling 10,563.76 ha (26,103.52 acres). &nbsp;Collectively the properties are known as the Contact Lake Mineral Claims.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Expenditures related to the Contact Lake Mineral Claims for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009, consist of amortization of $49,123 (2008 - $80,405), assaying and geochemical of $1,097 (2008 - $60,381), camp and field supplies of $109,729 (2008 - $138,769), claim maintenance and permitting of $260 (2008 - $4,359), community relations and government of $2,653 (2008 - $73,390), drilling of $12,304 (2008 - $153,576), &nbsp;equipment rental of $Nil (2008 - $3,590), geology and engineering of $28,682 (2008 - $204,678), &nbsp;geophysics of &nbsp;$Nil (2008 - $16,643), line cutting of &nbsp;$6,500 (2008 - $Nil), transportation and fuel of $176,595 (2008- $289,334), and wages, consulting and management fees of $522,071 (2008 - $538,627).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>During the year ended November 30, 2006, the Company acquired a 100% right, interest and title, subject to a 2% NSR, in eleven (11) mineral claims (the &#147;North Contact Lake Mineral Claims&#148;), for cash payments of $75,000 and the issue of 250,000 common shares of the Company valued at $182,500. &nbsp;The Company may purchase one-half of the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000. &nbsp;The North Contact Lake Mineral Claims are situated north of Contact Lake on Great Bear Lake approximately 680 km (423 miles) north of Yellowknife, NT, totalling 6,305.22 ha (15,580.48 acres).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Expenditures related to the North Contact Lake Mineral Claims for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009, consist of camp and field supplies of $Nil (2008 - $1,034), drilling of $Nil (2008 - $352,831), &nbsp;transportation and fuel of $Nil (2008- $9,606), and wages, consulting and management fees of $Nil (2008 - $9,887).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify><B>2.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><B>Port Radium &#150; Glacier Lake Mineral Claims, NT</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>During the year ended November 30, 2005, the Company acquired a 100% undivided right, title and interest, subject to a 2% NSR in four (4) mineral claims, totalling 2,520.78 ha (6,229.00 acres) (the &#147;Glacier Lake Mineral Claims&#148;) located one mile east of Port Radium on Great Bear Lake, NT. For cash payments of $30,000 (paid) and 360,000 common shares (issued and valued at $72,000) of the Company. &nbsp;The Company may purchase one-half of the NSR for a one-time payment of $1,000,000.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The property contains a fully operational all-season airstrip and base camp, situated at Glacier Lake. &nbsp;The Echo Bay claim (produced 23,779,178 ounces of silver) and the Port Radium &#150; Eldorado claim (produced 15 million pounds of uranium and 8 million ounces of silver). &nbsp;The Port Radium uranium belt was formerly one of Canada&#146;s principal producers of uranium during the 1930s and 1940s.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR>
<BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:3.333px; margin-bottom:3.333px" align=center>4</P>
<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<HR style="margin-top:9.6px; margin-bottom:9.6px" noshade size=1.333>
<P style="margin:3.667px; page-break-before:always" align=right><BR></P>
<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<P style="line-height:normal; margin:0px" align=justify>Expenditures related to the Glacier Lake Mineral Claims for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 consist of amortization of $6,278 (2008 - $7,612), assaying and geochemical of $Nil (2008 - $54,136), camp and field supplies of $Nil (2008 - $1,178), claim maintenance and permitting of $6,227 (2008 - $6,923), geology and engineering of $Nil (2008 - $36,206), transportation and fuel of $Nil (2008- $374,885), and wages, consulting and management fees of $Nil (2008 - $122,488).<FONT style="font-family:Arial; font-size:11pt"> &nbsp;</FONT></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin-top:0px; margin-bottom:-16px; padding-left:24px; text-indent:-24px" align=justify><B>3.</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px; padding-left:24px" align=justify><B>Eldorado South Project, NT</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>During the year ended November 30, 2007, the Company staked sixteen (16) claims (the &#147;Eldorado South Uranium Mineral Claims&#148;), and four (4) additional claims (the &#147;Eldorado West Uranium Mineral Claims&#148;) located ten miles south of Eldorado uranium mine on the east side of Great Bear Lake, NT and 680 km (423 miles) north of the city of Yellowknife, NT, collectively known as the Eldorado South Uranium Project. &nbsp;The Eldorado South Uranium Project now consist of thirty (30) mineral claims totaling 25,913.25 ha (64,032.78 acres).</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Eldorado South claims cover a radiometric anomaly that is over 3.5 kilometers in length and the expression suggests a potential near surface IOCG &amp; uranium target. &nbsp;The radiometric maps show a well defined uranium anomaly with a marked correlation of strong thorium (Th) and potassium (k) ratio patterns. &nbsp;The Eldorado South Anomaly has never been drill tested. &nbsp;The Eldorado South Anomaly was discovered as a result of the completion of a High Resolution, Multi-Parameter Regional radiometric and magnetic geophysical survey which was conducted in July 2006. &nbsp;The survey consisted of 16,708 line-kilometers at 100 meter line-spacing&#146;s. &nbsp;The purpose of the radiometric survey was to measure the gamma radiation field and locate prospective areas of high-grade uranium and poly-metallic deposition.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>In December 2007, the Deline Land Corporation passed a resolution placing a moratorium on any further uranium exploration and development on Deline District lands. &nbsp;The Deline Land Corporation has stated publicly and reiterated that all current agreements between the Deline Land Corporation and the Company would be fully honored. &nbsp;Several uranium mining moratoriums have been placed in several mining jurisdictions in Canada recently. &nbsp;They include a three year moratorium on uranium mining in Labrador (April 2008) and a moratorium issued in the Deline District (January 2008) in the Northwest Territories stating that they will not approve or consent to new uranium exploration or development until the 26 recommendations of the Canada-Deline Uranium Table have been addressed to the satisfaction of the leadership of the local community. &nbsp;The moratoriums do not apply to exploration for other minerals and mineral exploration activity is expected to continue in 
full force. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>On June 16, 2008, the Company completed its Community Consultation in the community of Deline and finalized an expanded TEK (Traditional Education Knowledge) study for the region. &nbsp;The Company&#146;s land-use permit application SO7C-008 was deemed completed by the Sahtu Land and Water Board.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>On July 14, 2008, the Company received final permit approval from the Sahtu Land and Water Board (SLWB) for the issuance of a third &#147;Class A&#148;- 5 year 75,000 meter drill permit (#S07C-008) for its Eldorado South Iron oxide, copper, gold, silver, and uranium project located in Canada&#146;s Northwest Territories. The Eldorado South permit (#S07C-008) is valid until July 10, 2013. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Expenditures related to the Eldorado South IOCG &amp; Uranium Mineral Claims for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 consist of camp costs and field supplies of $Nil (2008 - $7,822), claim maintenance and permitting of $10,762 (2008 - $46), &nbsp;community relations and government of $Nil (2008 - $3,555), equipment rental of $Nil (2008 - $9,901), geology and engineering of $71,193 (2008 - $84,048), staking and line cutting of $71,500 (2008 - $438,794), transportation and fuel of $Nil (2008 - $160,093) and wages, consulting and management fees of $48,942 (2008 - $144,046).</P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR>

<P style="margin:3.667px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><B>RESULTS OF OPERATIONS &#150; NINE MONTHS ENDED AUGUST 31, 2009</B></P>
<P style="margin:0px"><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>The Company&#146;s net loss for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 was $2,685,282 or $0.025 per share compared to a net loss of $5,193,345 or $0.05 per share for the nine month period ended August 31, 2008. &nbsp;The significant changes during the current fiscal period compared to the same period a year prior are as follows:</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Advertising and promotion expenses decreased $217,866 to $12,864 during the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 from the $230,730 during the same period a year prior. &nbsp;The decrease in advertising and promotion is primarily attributable to a reduction in advertising costs and news release dissemination.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Salaries and benefits for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 were $364,616 as compared to $417,317 for the nine month period ended August 31, 2008. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Stock-based compensation expense totalling $554,933, a non-cash item, was incurred during the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 for 3,950,000 stock options issued on July 3, 2009 and previously granted stock options that vested during the period as compared to $548,070 for the nine month period ended August 31, 2008. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Transfer fees and shareholder information costs decreased $138,060 to $190,430 for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 from $328,490 for the nine month period ended August 31, 2008. &nbsp;The decrease in transfer fees and shareholder information costs period over period is due mainly to decrease in fees and number of consultants used for the Company&#146;s investor relations and corporate development activities.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Travel expenses decreased $44,814 to $42,659 during the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 from $87,473 during the same period a year prior. &nbsp;This was due to decreased expenditures on trade show attendances and conferences during the current period.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>Interest income decreased $429,091 to $133,465 for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009, compared to $562,556 during the same period a year prior primarily due to the Company obtaining lower interest rates during the current period.</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify>A future income tax recovery of $104,300 for the nine month period ended August 31, 2009 was incurred as a result of recording the tax effect from the issuance of $350,000 in flow through shares which were renounced to the investors at December 31, 2008 but had not yet been spent on mineral property exploration. &nbsp;</P>
<P style="margin:0px" align=justify><BR></P>
